(TA.) And <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n7321-8" target="أثحْدُوثَةٌ" n="8" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>مَلِيحَةٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">A pretty story</hi>], and <foreign lang="ar">أَحَادِيثُ مِلَاحٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">pretty stories</hi>]. (A.) And   
      <foreign lang="ar">قَدْ صَارَ فُلَانٌ <ref cref="n7321-9" target="أَحْدُوثَةً" n="9" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [<tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">Such a one has become the subject of a story,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of a wonderful story:</hi> and in like manner, as is said in the A, <foreign lang="ar">صَارُوا أَحَادِيثَ</foreign>: there said to be tropical]. (IB, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Hence the <foreign lang="ar">حَدِيث</foreign> of the Apostle of God: (Msb:) [i. e.] <foreign lang="ar">حَدِيثٌ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">A narration of a</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مُحَدِّث</foreign>: (L:) [meaning <foreign lang="ar">حَدِيثٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">نَبَوِىٌّ</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">a tradition,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">narration, relating,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">describing, a saying</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an action &amp;c. of Mo- hammad:</hi>] this word and <foreign lang="ar">خَبَرٌ</foreign> both signify <hi rend="ital">a tradition that is traced up to Mohammad,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to a Sahábee,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to a Tábi'ee:</hi> (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">رقأ</foreign>:) or <foreign lang="ar">حديث</foreign> is applied to <hi rend="ital">what comes from the Prophet:</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">خَبَرٌ</foreign>, to what comes from another than the Prophet; or from him or another: and <foreign lang="ar">أَثَرٌ</foreign> to what comes from a Companion of the Prophet; but it may also be applied to a saying of the Prophet: (Kull p. 152:) the word in this sense, i. e. the <foreign lang="ar">حديث</foreign> of the Prophet, has for its pl. only <foreign lang="ar">أَحَادِيثُ</foreign>; and therefore Sb mentions it in the category of those words which have pls. anomalously formed; such as <foreign lang="ar">عَرُوضٌ</foreign>, pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَعَارِيضُ</foreign>; and <foreign lang="ar">بَاطِلٌ</foreign>, pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَبَاطِيلُ</foreign>. (TA.) [<foreign lang="ar">الحَدِيثَ</foreign> written at the end of a quotation of a part of a trad. is for <foreign lang="ar">اِقْرَأِ الحَدِيثَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Read the tradition.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">حَدِيثٌ قُدْسِىٌّ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">A holy tradition</hi> or <hi rend="ital">narration</hi>] means <hi rend="ital">what God has told to his prophet by inspiration,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by a dream,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in sleep, and the prophet has told in his own phraseology:</hi> the Kur-án is esteemed above this, because [it is held that] its words also were revealed: (KT:) <hi rend="ital">that of which the words are from the apostle, but the meaning is from God, by inspiration,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by a dream,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in sleep.</hi> (Kull p. 288.)    </entryFree>2e:T484,<entryFree id="n7333" key="مُحَدِّثٌ" type="main">

                  <hi rend="ital">A teller,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">relater, of stories, narratives,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">traditions:</hi> [and particularly <hi rend="ital">a relater of,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">one skilled in, the traditions of Mohammad:</hi>]   
      <anchor/><foreign lang="ar"><ref cref="n7333-1" target="حُدَّاثٌ" n="1" type="3" subtype="PO" lang="ar" select="n7323"/> </foreign> in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">مُحَدِّثُونَ</foreign>, signifying a company of men <hi rend="ital">telling,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">relating, stories</hi> &amp;c., is an anomalous pl., formed by assigning it to the same predicament as words of similar meaning, of which <foreign lang="ar">سُمَّارٌ</foreign>, pl. of <foreign lang="ar">سَامِرٌ</foreign>, is an ex.
